# Cgame Mapping Ledger

This ledger records the current reverse-engineered mapping pass for the retail
`cgamex86.dll` against `src/code/cgame/`. All claims below were checked against
the committed Ghidra corpus in `references/reverse-engineering/ghidra/cgamex86/`
and the Binary Ninja HLIL dump in `references/hlil/quakelive/cgamex86.dll/`.

Observed facts come from exports, function inventories, strings, and call flow.
Inferred names are only used where the retail behavior and the Quake Live source
analogue line up cleanly enough to support a stable mapping.

## Recovered Function Map

| Retail address | Recovered name | Closest source analogue | Evidence summary | Confidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `0x10020A70` | `dllEntry` | `cg_syscalls.c::dllEntry` | Named export in HLIL and Ghidra; installs the syscall table. | High |
| `0x10020A90` | `Com_Printf` | `cg_main.c::Com_Printf` | Varargs print wrapper wired into the retail `cgDC.Print` slot; HLIL forwards directly to `trap_Print`, which matches the narrower `Com_Printf` role better than source `CG_Printf` with its extra `cg_chatbeep` side path. | High |
| `0x10020AF0` | `Com_Error` | `cg_main.c::Com_Error` | Varargs error wrapper used across retail `cgame`, frequently called with Quake error levels, and assigned into `cgDC.Error` as the HUD/menu error callback. | High |
| `0x10020BB0` | `CG_RegisterCvars` | `cg_main.c::CG_RegisterCvars` | Iterates the retail cvar table, registers `model`, `headmodel`, and `cg_version`, then clears `ui_voteactive`; also appears as slot 1 in the native `cgame` entry table. | High |
| `0x10020CA0` | `CG_UpdateCvars` | `cg_main.c::CG_UpdateCvars` | Walks the retail cvar table with `trap_Cvar_Update`, checks tracked values, and triggers the refresh path used before `CG_DrawActiveFrame` continues. | High |
| `0x10020D60` | `CG_CrosshairPlayer` | `cg_main.c::CG_CrosshairPlayer` | Tiny native API-table helper returning the crosshair client index while the one-second timeout is still live. | High |
| `0x10020D80` | `CG_LastAttacker` | `cg_main.c::CG_LastAttacker` | Tiny native API-table helper returning the attacker persistent field while `cg.attackerTime` is active, otherwise `-1`. | High |
| `0x10007F00` | `CG_ConsoleCommand` | `cg_consolecmds.c::CG_ConsoleCommand` | Reads `Argv(0)`, scans the static console-command table, dispatches the matching handler, and returns `qtrue` or `qfalse`; HLIL also shows it exposed through the native entry table. | High |
| `0x10029820` | `CG_Init` | `cg_main.c::CG_Init` | HLIL-only function boundary with the retail startup sequence: version mismatch check, loading strings for `collision map`, `sounds`, `graphics`, `clients`, then the expected init calls, including the late `AdvertisementBridge_InitCGame` host import before the final looping-sound clear. Not present in committed `functions.csv`. | High |
| `0x10029FC0` | `CG_Shutdown` | `cg_main.c::CG_Shutdown` | Native entry-table slot that performs the retail teardown path, issues the shutdown-side advertisement-bridge syscall, and restores `ui_mainmenu` before returning. | High |
| `0x1003C6F0` | `CG_KeyEvent` | `cg_newdraw.c::CG_KeyEvent` | Two-argument input handler in the native entry table; HLIL fetches the bound command string and directly intercepts `messagemode`, `screenshot`, `screenshotJPEG`, `+voice`, and `+scores`, which is the retail key-input path for the spectator/HUD overlay. | High |
| `0x10020E70` | `CG_RegisterSounds` | `cg_main.c::CG_RegisterSounds` | Called from `CG_Init` after the retail loading string switches to `sounds`; body registers announcer, feedback, and weapon sounds. | High |
| `0x10022F40` | `CG_RegisterGraphics` | `cg_main.c::CG_RegisterGraphics` | Called from `CG_Init` after the retail loading string switches to `graphics`; body registers game media, shaders, and models. | High |
| `0x10025260` | `CG_RegisterClients` | `cg_main.c::CG_RegisterClients` | Called from `CG_Init` after the retail loading string switches to `clients`; loops player configstrings and registers client info. | High |
| `0x100252F0` | `CG_ConfigString` | `cg_main.c::CG_ConfigString` | Small bounds-checked accessor returning `gameState` string data. | High |
| `0x10025320` | `CG_StartMusic` | `cg_main.c::CG_StartMusic` | Reads the music configstring, parses two tokens, and starts the background track pair. | High |
| `0x10025CA0` | `CG_LoadMenus` | `cg_main.c::CG_LoadMenus` | Uses the menu-file fallback path, `ui/hud.txt`, size guards, `Menu_Reset`, `loadmenu`, and the UI menu load-time print. | High |
| `0x10028F30` | `CG_CacheScoreboardSelectionMenus` | `synthetic retail scoreboard-menu cache helper` | Caches the live and end-scoreboard menu roots for the current gametype after `CG_LoadMenus`; the paired cached pointers are then reused by the retail team-list selection callback. | High |
| `0x10029120` | `CG_LoadHudMenu` | `cg_main.c::CG_LoadHudMenu` | Reads `cg_hudFiles`, falls back to `ui/hud.txt`, calls `CG_LoadMenus`, and performs the loading half of the HUD bootstrap. | High |
| `0x10029210` | `CG_InitDisplayContext` | `synthetic retail cgDC bootstrap helper` | Deliberate synthetic retail name for the split HUD-display bootstrap. The committed Ghidra boundary and HLIL body both match the source-side `cgDC` callback assignment block from `CG_LoadHudMenu`, and the helper finishes by publishing `&cgDC` through the `ui_shared.c::Init_Display` context pointer. | High |
| `0x10029420` | `CG_AssetCache` | `cg_main.c::CG_AssetCache` | Registers gradient bar, scrollbar, and slider assets used by the HUD/menu path. | High |
| `0x100295C0` | `CG_SetGameInfoCvars` | `synthetic retail cg_gameInfo publisher` | Deliberate synthetic retail name for the six-line `cg_gameInfo*` helper. HLIL shows a training-text fast path plus a per-gametype six-column string table, with callsites from the HUD bootstrap and `CG_ParseServerinfo`. | High |
| `0x10019EB0` | `CG_EntityEvent` | `cg_event.c::CG_EntityEvent` | Large event switch with obituary, item, footstep, and unknown-event handling. | High |

| `0x10049980` | `CG_ConfigStringModified` | `cg_servercmds.c::CG_ConfigStringModified` | Reads `Argv(1)`, parses the changed configstring index, and switches over update handlers. This is not the plain `CG_ConfigString` accessor. | High |
| `0x1004A2E0` | `CG_MapRestart` | `cg_servercmds.c::CG_MapRestart` | Matches the map-restart reset path and the `CG_MapRestart` debug print. | High |
| `0x1004ADC0` | `CG_ServerCommand` | `cg_servercmds.c::CG_ServerCommand` | Main server-command dispatcher with `map_restart`, `clientLevelShot`, vote UI toggles, race commands, and the unknown-command print. | High |
| `0x1004C020` | `CG_TransitionSnapshot` | `cg_snapshot.c::CG_TransitionSnapshot` | Snapshot handoff with `NULL cg.snap` and `NULL cg.nextSnap` fatal paths. | High |
| `0x1004C4D0` | `CG_ProcessSnapshots` | `cg_snapshot.c::CG_ProcessSnapshots` | Snapshot pump with `latestSnapshotNum`, server-time ordering checks, and the handoff into `CG_TransitionSnapshot`. | High |
| `0x1004E4D0` | `CG_GetPhysicsTime` | `synthetic retail native export helper` | Deliberate synthetic native-export name for the one-word time getter. The host uses slot `data_146cc38 + 0x38` when formatting `[m:ss.mmm]` notify/chat prefixes, falling back to host `serverTime`; the retail body itself returns `cg.physicsTime`. | High |
| `0x1004E4E0` | `CG_DrawActiveFrame` | `cg_view.c::CG_DrawActiveFrame` | Top-level frame loop that updates cvars, clears scene state, calls `CG_ProcessSnapshots`, runs prediction, and builds the view. | High |

### Retail Event Helper Sweep

- The event-side tranche now includes `CG_PlaceString`, `CG_Obituary`, `CG_UseItem`, `CG_PainEvent`, and the synthetic retail helper `CG_TryAutoFollowPowerup`. That closes the most distinctive standalone helpers under `CG_EntityEvent` without forcing unstable names onto the smaller retail-only sidecars in the same region.
- `CG_Obituary` is now closer to the retail feed shape as well as the retail event behavior: the current source caches expanded obituary rows with target/attacker strings, per-name color ids, icon handles, row-cap trimming through `cg_obituaryRowSize`, and expiry compaction instead of rebuilding every line from only `(attacker, target, mod, time)` at draw time.
- `CG_TryAutoFollowPowerup` is intentionally documented as a synthetic retail name rather than being flattened onto a GPL helper. The current source split still keeps the newer tracked-player overlay state, but it now mirrors the retail direct follow-command shape: `cg_event.c` still feeds powerup/flag spectator tracking through `CG_TrackFlagCarrierForEvent` and `CG_SpectatorTrackEvent`, and the follow path now emits `follow %d%s` with the optional `" pw"` suffix on the direct powerup-pickup path.

### Retail HUD Status/Text Sweep

- The ownerdraw text/status sweep now covers the broader `0x10032110-0x10034D70` cluster: `CG_DrawKiller`, `CG_GetScoreboardTimerSeconds`, `CG_DrawCapFragLimit`, `CG_DrawClanArenaPlayers`, `CG_DrawPlayerCount`, `CG_DrawRoundLabel`, `CG_DrawDominationOwnedFlags`, `CG_DrawGameLimit`, `CG_DrawGameTypeIcon`, `CG_DrawFirstPlaceModel`, `CG_DrawPlayerModel`, `CG_GetGameStatusText`, `CG_DrawGameStatus`, `CG_DrawGameType`, `CG_DrawMatchStatus`, and `CG_DrawSpectatorMessages`.
- `0x10034A00` is intentionally normalized as the synthetic `CG_GetMatchStatusText` rather than forced onto a GPL symbol. Retail composes the uppercase match-phase label plus the status suffix there, and the current source tree now mirrors that split instead of building the buffer inline inside `CG_DrawMatchStatus`.
- `CG_GetGameStatusText` now also follows the narrower retail status family: Race returns no status suffix, Red Rover stays on the placement path, and team modes use the colorized `^1Red^7` / `^4Blue^7` lead strings instead of the older plain-text wording.
- The tranche also explains the earlier `Fragged by %s` width anchor: `0x10032110` is the actual `CG_DrawKiller` ownerdraw, while both the draw helper and `CG_OwnerDrawWidth` inline the killer-text formatting instead of calling a standalone `CG_GetKillerText`.
- `CG_DrawGameTypeIcon` now stays source-aligned at the asset-path level too: retail draws pre-registered `.tga` handles from `CG_RegisterGraphics`, and the current source now mirrors that registration path instead of lazily registering `.png` assets on demand.
- `CG_DrawGameLimit` is still worth calling out because HLIL preserves the exact `Cap Limit` / `Frag Limit` / `Round Limit` / `Score Limit` string family behind ownerdraw case `CG_GAME_LIMIT`; the current source helper now mirrors that narrower retail label set instead of the earlier broader summary text.
- `CG_DrawSpectatorMessages` is now source-aligned to the older retail copy family: `Round In Progress`, `SPECTATOR MODE`, `waiting to play`, the join-button fallback, and the mouse-cycle hint all ride the same HUD slot.
- `0x10034900` and `0x10034980` now form a stable paired profile-image recovery. `CG_DrawFirstPlaceModel` stays aligned to `CG_1STPLACE_PLYR_MODEL`, while `CG_DrawPlayerModel` keeps the separate retail `CG_PLAYERMODEL` slot explicit and is now wired through the source-side ownerdraw switch.
- Rechecking the retail `CG_OwnerDraw` switch corrected the `CG_DrawPlayerModel` case anchor from the stale `0x1A` note to the actual `0x25` / `CG_PLAYERMODEL` ownerdraw id; the source helper already existed, but the dispatch case was missing.
- The source-side parity test now extracts the committed `FUN_1003B0F0` retail switch, resolves named ownerdraw ids through `src/ui/menudef.h`, and verifies each named retail case is covered by either a direct `CG_OwnerDraw` case or the pre-switch placement/award helper ranges. That keeps future ownerdraw wiring sweeps mechanical instead of relying on manual menu-token scans.

### Retail Intro / Endgame Ownerdraw Sweep

- The intro/endgame panel tranche now also covers `CG_DrawLevelTimer`, `CG_DrawStartingWeapons`, `CG_DrawLocalTime`, `CG_DrawMatchEndCondition`, `CG_DrawMapName`, `CG_DrawMatchDetails`, `CG_DrawGameTypeMap`, `CG_DrawSelectedPlayerAccuracy`, `CG_DrawSelectedPlayerBestWeapon`, and `CG_DrawEndGameScore`.
- `CG_DrawStartingWeapons` is now source-aligned to the retail intro panel path: the helper prefers `CS_LOADOUT_MASK`, renders the icon strip in retail weapon order, and appends the queued-primary preview after the `+` separator.
- `CG_DrawLocalTime` is likewise source-aligned now that the public helper prints the full local date/time label with month/day/year instead of the older `HH:MM` output.
- `CG_DrawMatchDetails` and `CG_DrawGameTypeMap` both reuse the same prebuilt panel string in retail, and the current source helpers now follow those shorter retail format shapes.
- `CG_DrawEndGameScore` is now source-aligned to the richer retail summary family behind `CG_PLYR_END_GAME_SCORE`: the current helper follows the `You finished ...`, `You had %d assist%s.`, `You had %d defend%s.`, `You had %d flag capture%s.`, `You captured %d skull%s.`, and forfeit branches instead of the older generic score strings.
- `CG_MATCH_WINNER` also stays closer to retail now on the intermission/forfeit edge: the current helper preserves the retail `...^7 WINS by forfeit` wording instead of flattening every winner line into `Winner: ...`.
- The team pickup/time-held ownerdraws now stay on the retail telemetry path too: current source consumes the parsed `scorestats_team` payload directly, preserves the published field count, and no longer synthesizes `CG_TEAMSTAT_MAP_PICKUPS` from scoreboard-side capture/assist/defend proxies when that payload is absent.

### HUD Callback Bridge At `0x10029210`

- `0x10029210` is now stable enough to promote as the synthetic retail helper `CG_InitDisplayContext`. The committed Ghidra corpus already carries a standalone function boundary there, HLIL shows the full `cgDC` callback slab being wired at that address, and the tail write to `data_1074ccf8` matches the source-side `Init_Display(&cgDC)` handoff from `ui_shared.c`.
- The front drawtools tranche is now explicit too: retail `0x100122B0`, `0x100123C0`, `0x100123D0`, `0x10012460`, `0x10012540`, `0x10012620`, and `0x100126A0` line up cleanly with `CG_AdjustFrom640`, `CG_SetAdjustFrom640Mode`, `CG_FillRect`, `CG_DrawSides`, `CG_DrawTopBottom`, `CG_DrawRect`, and `CG_DrawPic`. The recovered `cgDC` tail and the shared menu callsites show the same helper pair the current source now exposes through `adjustFrom640` and `setAdjustFrom640Mode`.
- `0x10031790 -> CG_OwnerDrawVisible` keeps a two-word callback contract. Ghidra exposes the retail body as `FUN_10031790(uint param_1,uint param_2)`, with `param_1` covering the primary `ownerdrawflag` constants and `param_2` covering Quake Live's secondary `ownerdrawflag2` constants. The shared menu paint paths now pass both words together so secondary bits such as `CG_SHOW_IF_PLYR1` (`0x00000001`) no longer collide with primary bits such as `CG_SHOW_BLUE_TEAM_HAS_REDFLAG` (`0x00000001`).
- The same retail visibility body also keeps `CG_SHOW_IF_CHAT_VISIBLE` live when either the chat-history latch (`data_10a9c9b4`) is set or the scoreboard menu pass returned visible (`data_10aa6934`). Current source mirrors that with `cg.chatHistoryVisible || cg.scoreBoardShowing`, preserving scoreboard chat rows even when the explicit chat-history latch is not held.
- The `CG_SHOW_IF_MSG_PRESENT` / `CG_SHOW_IF_NOTICE_PRESENT` bits are not raw string-presence checks in retail. HLIL reads `data_10a5f2f8` / `data_10a5f2fc`, returns false when the selected timeout is zero, and only shows the icon while `(cg.time & 0x200)` is set. The only committed writes arm those fields at `0x10029FF0` / `0x1002A060` for `cg.time + 3000`, so current source now reuses the tracked-slot latch timers for the blinking notification icons.
- The duel scoreboard `CG_SHOW_IF_*_FIRED` bits are likewise score-cache predicates, not local inventory checks. Retail `CG_OwnerDrawVisible` tests the first two placement rows' copied weapon-stat arrays: gauntlet uses the fourth per-weapon field, while MG through HMG use the second per-weapon field. Current source mirrors that with `CG_PlacementWeaponFired`, mapping the fields onto the parsed placement `weaponShots[WP_GAUNTLET]` and `weaponDamage[*]` cache entries instead of `ps.stats[STAT_WEAPONS]`.
- `CG_OwnerDrawVisible` stays in the cgame display-flag namespace. The earlier source-side attempt to accept `UI_SHOW_*` aliases in the cgame primary word collided with retail `CG_SHOW_*` bits (`UI_SHOW_ANYTEAMGAME == CG_SHOW_CTF`, `UI_SHOW_IF_WARMUP == CG_SHOW_TEAMINFO`, and so on), so the cgame predicate now leaves those UI-only tokens to `ui_main.c::UI_OwnerDrawVisible`.
- This pass keeps the paired print/error hooks explicit in the bridge notes: `0x10020A90` is now normalized as `Com_Printf` because source `cg_main.c` wires `cgDC.Print = &Com_Printf`, and retail HLIL shows a direct `trap_Print` wrapper with no `cg_chatbeep` branch; `0x10020AF0` remains `Com_Error` because retail call sites preserve the leading Quake error-level parameter before forwarding through `cgDC.Error`.
- The bridge coverage now includes the remaining high-confidence value/text/feeder/cinematic targets: `CG_Cvar_Get`, the deliberately named `CG_Cvar_GetString` adaptor, `CG_Text_PaintWithCursor`, `CG_OwnerDrawHandleKey`, `CG_FeederCount`, `CG_FeederItemText`, `CG_FeederSelection`, `CG_OwnerDrawWidth`, `CG_PlayCinematic`, `CG_StopCinematic`, `CG_DrawCinematic`, and `CG_RunCinematicFrame`, alongside the already-mapped `CG_OwnerDraw`, `CG_GetValue`, `CG_OwnerDrawVisible`, `CG_RunMenuScript`, and `CG_GetTeamColor`. The retail `cgDC.feederItemImage` slot is still accounted for, but HLIL shows it reusing the same `qfalse` stub as `CG_OwnerDrawHandleKey` rather than a dedicated feeder-image body.
- `CG_Cvar_GetString` is intentionally documented as a synthetic retail adapter name rather than a public-source symbol. The stable part is the callback contract: token-helper fast path first, `trap_Cvar_VariableStringBuffer` fallback otherwise.
- `CG_DrawCinematic` is also a slightly unusual recovery: the committed corpus still does not expose a clean standalone function start, but the direct `cgDC.drawCinematic` slot assignment plus the extents-then-draw syscall sequence make the callback role itself stable enough to normalize.
- `CG_InitDisplayContext` is intentionally documented as a synthetic retail name rather than being flattened onto a source symbol. Current source still inlines that bootstrap inside `CG_LoadHudMenu`, while retail split it into a dedicated helper before the HUD file load runs.

### Retail Buffered Chat Stack

- HLIL exposes a small retail-only chat-stack cluster around `data_10079840`: `0x100068E0` clears the active slot plus the 24-entry history ring, `CG_PushPrintString` at `0x10006910` pushes a timed entry into that ring, and `0x10006A10` renders the stack from ownerdraw case `CG_AREA_NEW_CHAT`.
- The retail command-table tail now makes the latch explicit: `0x10007CD0` (`+chat`) sets `data_10a9c9b4`, `0x10007CF0` (`-chat`) clears it, and `0x10007D10` (`togglechathistory`) flips it. `0x10006A10` checks that same latch to decide whether the full buffered history should stay visible.
- `0x10007D30` is the retail `print` front-end into that stack, while `CG_PushPrintString` is the underlying timed-buffer writer used by `print`, `chat`, `tchat`, `bchat`, and the tracked-slot notifier pair.
- `CG_Show1stTrackedPlayer` and `CG_Show2ndTrackedPlayer` are intentionally synthetic names for that notifier pair: both read `cg_lastmsg` into the chat ring, but they also arm the tracked-slot timers consumed by the spectator slot-highlight drawing path. Retail `CG_OwnerDrawVisible` does not expose separate `CG_SHOW_IF_*_PLYR_TRACKED` `ownerdrawflag2` bits; the shipped flag word stops at `CG_SHOW_IF_2ND_PLYR_FOLLOWED`.
- The notifier pair is intentionally unconditional apart from the 0/1 slot selector: HLIL for `0x10029FF0` and `0x1002A060` sets the timer, fetches `cg_lastmsg`, and calls `CG_PushPrintString` without checking whether the current spectator slot has a valid clientInfo record. Current source now follows that export shape, while the draw-time slot highlight path still handles missing slot data defensively.
- `CG_PushPrintString` is intentionally documented as a synthetic retail helper rather than flattened into the public-source `CG_SetPrintString`: the stable behavior is the timed history-ring push, not the older flat-string contract.
- Current source now mirrors the public-facing part of that retail stack: `cg_consolecmds.c` exposes `+chat`, `-chat`, `togglechathistory`, and `print`; `cg_newdraw.c::CG_DrawNewChatArea` obeys the same history latch instead of always painting the full ring; `cg_main.c::CG_PushPrintString` feeds `print`, `chat`, `tchat`, voice-text replay, and `cg_lastmsg` persistence through the shared timed chat buffer; and `cg_servercmds.c` now consumes the retail `bchat` and `clearChat` server commands instead of dropping them.

### Command Table Sweep At `data_10078DC0`

- The static command table now yields a large source-identical recovery set instead of just the earlier tail cluster: `CG_TargetCommand_f`, `CG_SizeUp_f`, `CG_SizeDown_f`, `CG_Viewpos_f`, `CG_ScoresDown_f`, `CG_ScoresUp_f`, `CG_TellTarget_f`, `CG_TellAttacker_f`, `CG_VoiceTellTarget_f`, `CG_VoiceTellAttacker_f`, the `nextTeamMember` / `prevTeamMember` pair, the order-confirm / deny flow, and the full task / taunt family through `CG_TaskSuicide_f`.
- `0x10006E40` is no longer treated as an anonymous loader clone. The command-table slot, `cg_hudFiles` / `ui/hud.txt` reads, parser reset, and `CG_LoadMenus` replay make it stable as the retail `CG_LoadHud_f` wrapper.
- Cross-file command targets are now also stable from the same table: `CG_LoadDeferredPlayers`, `CG_ZoomDown_f`, `CG_ZoomUp_f`, `CG_NextWeapon_f`, `CG_PrevWeapon_f`, and `CG_Weapon_f`. The weapon path is source-aligned but retail extends it with a `toggle` argument.
- Retail-only wrappers recovered from the same sweep now include `CG_DropFlag_f`, `CG_DropPowerup_f`, `CG_DropRune_f`, `CG_DropWeapon_f`, `CG_ReadyUp_f`, `CG_Team_f`, `CG_Forfeit_f`, `CG_RageQuit_f`, `CG_SetTeamColor_f`, and `CG_SetEnemyColor_f`.
- The command-table tail findings still stand: `CG_StartOrbit_f`, the three chat-history handlers, the buffered `CG_Print_f` front-end, and `CG_ClientMute_f` remain stable, while the private native mute/social callback stays an observed import-table extension rather than a forced public enum slot.
- Current source now mirrors that narrower retail local console surface: `CG_ConsoleCommand` keeps `nextTeamMember` / `prevTeamMember`, while spectator follow or camera actions stay on the `CG_RunMenuScript` path instead of extra dedicated console strings.
- Current source now mirrors the retail local wrapper cluster for the drop and concession tail too: `cg_consolecmds.c` handles `dropflag`, `droppowerup`, `droprune`, `dropweapon`, `forfeit`, and `ragequit` locally with the same gametype and InstaGib gates before forwarding to the server, and `ragequit` now arms the existing `cg.rageQuitTime` countdown latch instead of bypassing it.
- Current source now mirrors the retail local color-wrapper pair too: `setteamcolor` and `setenemycolor` live in `cg_consolecmds.c`, preserve the raw 1-3 character token through `cg_teamColors` / `cg_enemyColors`, and apply the recovered retail 26-entry palette onto the per-part head/upper/lower override cvars in the same upper/lower/head token order observed in HLIL.
- Current source now mirrors the retail local `team` and `readyup` wrappers too: `cg_consolecmds.c` formats `team %s`, forwards it through `trap_SendClientCommand`, and then dismisses the cgame-owned capture state by clearing `CGAME_EVENT_TEAMMENU` / `CGAME_EVENT_EDITHUD` and dropping `KEYCATCH_CGAME`; `readyup` now also stays local, requiring an active warmup or ready-up deadline and blocking spectators unless the recovered intermission bypass is active before forwarding to the server.
- Retail `0x10007840` no longer needs a proxy-only explanation. HLIL shows the special-case bypass keying off the same `pm_type` family used by the match-status helpers, with `5` resolving to `PM_INTERMISSION` in [`bg_public.h`](../../src/code/game/bg_public.h). Current source now mirrors that by reading the live or predicted `pm_type` instead of consulting tutorial configstrings or `g_training`.
- `CG_InitConsoleCommands` now also registers the missing retail forwarded-command tail instead of the older shorter GPL-era set, including `abort`, `ban`, `dropflag`, `dropweapon`, `forfeit`, `listaccess`, `lock`, `mute`, `put`, `ragequit`, `reload_access`, `setmatchtime`, `spec`, `tempban`, `timein`, `timeout`, `unlock`, `unmute`, and `unpause`.
- The taunt sweep also clarifies one small retail/source divergence: retail dispatches `kill_gauntlet`, not the public-source typo `kill_guantlet`.

### Native Import Extensions Used By `cgDC`

The reconstructed export therefore preserves the observed zero transport discriminator while still mirroring the retail identity words and names.
- `CG_ClientMute_f` and the `ui_priv` server-command path both reinforce that retail `cgame` talks to additional native social callbacks that are absent from the current public import enum: `+0x1F8` mutates mute state, while `ui_priv` remains an observed bridge rather than a normalized server-command analogue.

- `CG_GetChatFieldY` at `0x100209E0` and `CG_GetChatFieldPixelWidth` at `0x10020A00` are now stable enough to normalize as synthetic native-export names: the host chat-input draw path at `0x004B4100` calls slots `data_146cc38 + 0x44` and `+ 0x48` before its `SCR_AdjustFrom640`-style scaler, while retail returns `413 / 455` and `640 / 300` depending on `data_10a9c214`.

- `CG_GetPhysicsTime` at `0x1004E4D0` closes the last unnamed native-export getter in this sidecar cluster. The host timestamp-prefix path uses slot `data_146cc38 + 0x38` and falls back to host `serverTime`, while the retail body itself is the one-word read of `cg.physicsTime`.

### Server Settings / Scoreboard Parser Sweep

- This mapping pass lands the next cgame tranche across the ownerdraw settings panel and the retail scoreboard transport family: `CG_DrawServerSettings`, the retail-aligned `CG_ParseFFAScores`, `CG_ParseDuelScores`, and `CG_ParseClanArenaScores`, plus the source-identical `CG_ParseRaceScores`, `CG_ParseTdmScores`, `CG_ParseCtfScores`, and `CG_ParseFreezeScores`.

- The scoreboard parser family now lines up cleanly with retail server-command transport names. `CG_ServerCommand` dispatches `scores_ffa`, `scores_duel`, `scores_race`, `scores_tdm`, `scores_ca`, `scores_ctf`, and `scores_ft` into seven dedicated functions, and the qagame mapping already carries the paired serializers `G_BuildFFAScoreboardMessage`, `G_BuildDuelScoreboardMessage`, `G_BuildRaceScoreboardMessage`, `G_BuildTeamScoreboardMessage`, `G_BuildClanArenaScoreboardMessage`, `G_BuildCTFStyleScoreboardMessage`, and `G_BuildFreezeScoreboardMessage`.
- The three synthetic names are deliberate. Current source now preserves the retail-specific `CG_ParseFFAScores` entry point for `scores_ffa` while still carrying the legacy generic `CG_ParseScores` path for `scores`; the retail command split, the qagame-side transport names, and the distinct payload layouts remain the strongest evidence for keeping the Quake Live-specific parser roles as `CG_ParseFFAScores`, `CG_ParseDuelScores`, and `CG_ParseClanArenaScores`.
- `CG_ParseDuelScores` now consumes the 14 weapon blocks in the same classic item-tag order exposed by the retail HLIL loop: G, MG, SG, GL, RL, LG, RG, PG, BFG, grappling hook, NG, PL, CG, HMG. This matters because the HUD-visible duel weapon rows skip the grappling slot but still expect NG/PL/CG/HMG to land after it; walking the current `weapon_t` enum would shift SG/HMG-family data before `CG_OwnerDrawVisible` and the placement ownerdraws can read it.
- Before this round, the current cgame map held `181` named addresses: `104 / 751` committed Ghidra functions (`13.8%`) plus `77` HLIL-only anchors for `181 / 828` combined committed anchors (`21.9%`). After this round, the map holds `189` named addresses: `112 / 751` committed Ghidra functions (`14.9%`) plus the same `77` HLIL-only anchors for `189 / 828` combined committed anchors (`22.8%`).

Good Game` states that feed back into the warmup banner logic.
- The synthetic names in this tranche are deliberate. The GPL-derived tree still keeps most of this behavior either inline in `CG_DrawWarmup`, inside generic score parsers, or absent entirely, while the retail binary exposes stable standalone helpers whose boundaries are clearer than any forced source-identical rename.

## Important Disagreements And Split Paths

### Export disagreement: `dllEntry` vs `entry`

- Ghidra `exports.txt` lists both `0x10020A70 dllEntry` and `0x10063D56 entry`.
- HLIL shows the PE export table naming only `dllEntry` at `0x10020A70`.
- HLIL also shows `addressOfEntryPoint = 0x63D56`, which makes `0x10063D56`
  the PE entrypoint / CRT startup rather than a named export.
- Current working assumption: treat `dllEntry` as the only named export and
  record `entry` as a Ghidra corpus disagreement, not as a normalized symbol.

### HLIL-only `CG_Init` boundary at `0x10029820`

- HLIL presents a clean function boundary at `0x10029820`.
- The committed Ghidra `functions.csv` and `analysis_symbols.txt` do not contain
  a function start at `0x10029820`.
- The internal flow still matches `CG_Init` strongly enough to map it, but the
  discrepancy should be preserved until the corpus is refreshed.

### Native API version / slot-order mismatch

- The current source path in `win_main.c::Sys_LoadDll` and `vm.c::VM_CallNativeExports`
  supports native game DLLs returning an export array plus an API version instead
  of the old `vmMain`-only contract.
- Retail `cgame` uses that path: HLIL `dllEntry` stores `&data_100769A8` into the
  export pointer and writes `8` to the caller-provided `apiVersion`.
- `src/code/cgame/cg_public.h` still describes the legacy `cgameExport_t` order.
- Current mapping policy: do not force `data_100769A8` into a source-identical slot
  order until each retail slot is revalidated against direct behavior.

### Split HUD bootstrap

- The source-level `CG_LoadHudMenu` is not monolithic in retail.
- `0x10029120` performs the shared menu-selection and load phase used during init.
- `0x10029210` now resolves as the synthetic retail helper `CG_InitDisplayContext`, which wires the `cgDC` callbacks and then publishes the display context through the same `Init_Display(&cgDC)` step that current source still keeps inline.
- `0x10006E40`, referenced via `data_10078E5C`, now resolves as the retail
  `CG_LoadHud_f` console wrapper that replays that same HUD load path on demand.
- Current mapping policy: normalize `0x10029120` as `CG_LoadHudMenu`,
  `0x10029210` as the synthetic `CG_InitDisplayContext`, and `0x10006E40`
  as `CG_LoadHud_f`, while still avoiding false public-source symbol claims
  for the retail split itself.

### Retail Weapon-Reload Configstring Sweep

- This pass promotes `0x100492E0` as `CG_ParseWeaponReloadConfigString`.
- The evidence chain is direct and high-confidence: `CG_ConfigStringModified` dispatches `0x2AB` to `0x100492E0`, `CG_SetConfigValues` calls the same helper during bootstrap, and HLIL shows 14 straight `atoi(sub_10057620())` writes into `0x100790A0 .. 0x10079310`.
- Those 14 destinations are the `+0x10` reload fields inside the contiguous 0x30 retail weapon descriptor slab: gauntlet, machinegun, shotgun, grenade launcher, rocket launcher, lightning gun, railgun, plasmagun, BFG, grappling hook, nailgun, prox launcher, chaingun, and heavy machinegun.
- The recovered values line up with the retail refire defaults already exposed by the table itself, and they also close two lingering source mismatches: grappling hook is `200` rather than `100`, and heavy machinegun is `80` rather than `75`.
- Source reconstruction now publishes a dedicated `CS_WEAPON_RELOAD_TIMES` payload from `g_main.c`, parses it in `cg_servercmds.c`, overwrites the matching `cg_pmoveSettings.weaponReloadTimes[]` entries in retail order, and uses the recovered railgun refire duration in `CG_AddPlayerWeapon` instead of the older hardcoded `1500` fallback.

### Retail Match-State Auxiliary Sweep

- This pass promotes `0x10048C80` as `CG_ParseMatchState`.
- The recovery is high-confidence from the surrounding call graph alone: `CG_ConfigStringModified` dispatches `CS_MATCH_STATE` (`0x295`) to `0x10048C80`, and `CG_SetConfigValues` calls the same helper during bootstrap before the adjacent timeout/team-count auxiliary slots are refreshed.
- The committed Ghidra body is compact because the retail helper only consumes the round-state core directly from `CS_MATCH_STATE`: transition time, round number, turn marker, and state. The surrounding cgame handler then reacts to the dedicated `CS_TEAM_COUNT_RED` / `CS_TEAM_COUNT_BLUE` and `CS_TIMEOUT_START_TIME` / `CS_TIMEOUT_EXPIRE_TIME` / `CS_TIMEOUT_COUNT_RED` / `CS_TIMEOUT_COUNT_BLUE` side channels as those configstrings change.
- Source reconstruction now mirrors that split more closely. `cg_servercmds.c` parses the timeout/team-count auxiliaries through dedicated helpers during bootstrap and on live configstring updates, `cg_event.c` freezes the match clock at `CS_TIMEOUT_START_TIME` when the server enters an indefinite timeout, and `cg_newdraw.c` falls back to a plain `Timeout <team>` label until `timein` publishes a real expiry countdown.

### Retail Spectator / Medal / Advert HUD Sweep

- This pass promotes five committed cgame ownerdraw helpers from the adjacent HUD seam: `0x100350C0 -> CG_DrawSpeedometerOwnerDraw`, `0x100351A0 -> CG_DrawTeamSpectators`, `0x10035340 -> CG_DrawMedal`, `0x10035540 -> CG_DrawAdvert`, and `0x10037F80 -> CG_DrawTeamPickupOwnerDraw`.
- `0x100350C0` is the narrow retail `CG_SPEEDOMETER` leaf rather than the broader source helper. HLIL shows the function doing exactly one job: sampling the cached speedometer value, formatting it through `%i`, centering the text in the ownerdraw rect, and painting it. That is why the stable normalized name is the deliberate split `CG_DrawSpeedometerOwnerDraw` instead of reusing the earlier wider `CG_DrawSpeedometer` mapping.
- `0x100351A0` is the real `CG_SPECTATORS` ownerdraw, and the existing placeholder source implementation was too narrow. The committed body pages through a rect-bounded slice of the spectator-name list, measures how many names fit horizontally, paints them along the HUD baseline with fixed spacing, and only then advances the starting index on a timed cadence. Source reconstruction now follows that paged spectator-list behavior instead of printing only primary and secondary tracked-player labels.

### Retail Cgame Math / Mark-Axis Sweep

- This pass promotes ten more committed helper starts from the local `q_math` corridor compiled into `cgamex86.dll`: `0x10056450 -> RotatePointAroundVector`, `0x10056780 -> RotateAroundDirection`, `0x100568A0 -> vectoangles`, `0x10056A70 -> ProjectPointOnPlane`, `0x10056B40 -> LerpAngle`, `0x10056BC0 -> AngleSubtract`, `0x10056C40 -> VectorNormalize`, `0x10056CD0 -> VectorNormalize2`, `0x10056D60 -> MatrixMultiply`, and `0x10056E40 -> AngleVectors`.
- The evidence chain is straightforward because the bodies line up 1:1 with `q_math.c`. `0x10056CD0` is the copy-normalizing helper used by `CG_ImpactMark` and other render/effect paths, `0x10056C40` is the in-place normalizer, `0x10056A70` projects a point onto the plane defined by a normal, and `0x10056450` builds the same basis / z-rotation matrices and rotates a point around a direction vector exactly like `RotatePointAroundVector`. The adjacent `0x10056780` then rebuilds an axis with `PerpendicularVector`, optional yaw rotation, and a closing cross product, which matches `RotateAroundDirection`.
- The rest of the corridor is equally direct. `0x100568A0` preserves the familiar vector-to-Euler `atan2` path and final `PITCH/YAW/ROLL` layout from `vectoangles`; `0x10056B40` and `0x10056BC0` match the wrapped-angle logic from `LerpAngle` and `AngleSubtract`; `0x10056D60` is the explicit 3x3 matrix multiply; and `0x10056E40` computes the same forward/right/up basis from yaw, pitch, and roll that `AngleVectors` emits in public source.
- Source reconstruction now mirrors the retail mark-axis split in `cg_marks.c`: `CG_ImpactMark` no longer keeps the axis-orientation chain inline, and instead routes through a local `CG_BuildMarkAxis` helper that directly stages the same `VectorNormalize2 -> PerpendicularVector -> RotatePointAroundVector -> CrossProduct` sequence observed in HLIL.
- The live committed corpus in `references/reverse-engineering/ghidra/cgamex86/functions.csv` currently contains `751` starts, so this round is reported against `751 / 851`.

### Retail Bg Pmove Step-Jump / Air-Control Sidecar Sweep

- This pass promotes seven more committed cgame starts from the remaining movement sidecar corridor: synthetic `0x10001EC0 -> PM_LoadMoveTuningConstants`, synthetic `0x100025E0 -> PM_BuildWishMove3D`, synthetic `0x10002790 -> PM_ApplyJumpTakeoff`, synthetic `0x10002990 -> PM_CanCrouchStepJump`, synthetic `0x100029E0 -> PM_CanStepJump`, `0x10004070 -> PM_AirControl`, and `0x100050B0 -> PM_CorrectAllSolid`.

- The second evidence chain closes the shared jump and air-control helpers. `0x10002790` is the same `PM_ApplyJumpTakeoff` body as qagame `0x1002E2C0`: it resets the ground state, computes the final vertical takeoff speed from the cached jump timing mode, emits `EV_JUMP`, updates the last-jump timestamp, and selects the forward/back jump animation, all from a leaf reached by both `PM_CheckJump` and the step-jump path. `0x10004180` keeps the mode-specific airstop, strafe, and `pm_wishspeed` handling inside `PM_AirMove` before the generic `PM_Accelerate` call, while `0x10004070` is the retail `PM_AirControl` leaf beneath it: it strips Z, normalizes planar velocity, applies the same `32 * airControl * dot^2 * frametime` steering term, renormalizes, and restores the preserved vertical speed.

Both cgame leaves read the recovered `autoHop` slot for held-jump release bypasses and leave the adjacent `bunnyHop` slot out of that decision, matching qagame `0x1002E510` and `0x1002E590`.

- The 2026-05-22 transport follow-up keeps `pmove_ChainJump` as the recovered integer jump-mode selector instead of a boolean mirror. Server publication, cgame compact parsing, and the legacy JSON fallback now preserve mode `0`/`1`/`2`, so the shared `PM_ApplyJumpTakeoff` leaf can reach the disabled, gradient, and additive branches that the retail mode global exposes.
- The last two starts close the remaining sidecar utility leaves around that seam. `0x100050B0` is exact `PM_CorrectAllSolid`, anchored by the `\"%i:allsolid\\n\"` diagnostic and the same 3x3x3 jitter probe used by the public source. `0x10001EC0` and `0x100025E0` remain deliberate synthetic names, but their roles are stable: the first seeds one of two retail move-constant bundles right at the top of `PmoveSingle`, and the second builds and normalizes the shared 3D wish-move vector consumed by the water/fly/ladder corridor.

### Retail Queued World-Marker Sweep

- This pass promotes three more committed cgame starts from the shared retail queued world-marker seam still missing from the public-source reconstruction: synthetic `0x10011680 -> CG_DrawQueuedWorldMarkers`, synthetic `0x1002A0D0 -> CG_AllocQueuedWorldMarker`, and synthetic `0x1002A190 -> CG_UpdateQueuedWorldMarkers`.
- The allocator evidence is the cleanest starting point. `0x1002A0D0` is reached from the already-mapped synthetic `CG_DamagePlum`, the `EV_POI` event case, the race start/checkpoint indicator corridor, `CG_PlayerObjectiveSprite`, and several entity-side status-marker producers. Every caller receives either a free `0x80`-byte record from the same `32`-entry slab or a null result on exhaustion, then writes the same type/origin/color/payload fields before returning, so the narrow stable role is a shared queued world-marker allocator rather than a plum-only helper.
- The paired update and draw passes line up directly with that allocator. `0x1002A190` runs from `CG_DrawActiveFrame` before snapshot/view work continues, walks the same slab in four-record batches, clears expired active bits, and recomputes live fade alpha from each record's start/duration/fade-window fields. `0x10011680` is the consumer reached from the active render path: HLIL rejects behind-camera or inactive records, projects the surviving world origins into screen space, and then renders the optional text and sprite payloads used by the retail damage-plum, `EV_POI`, race checkpoint, and objective-indicator seams.
- This also closes the explicit gap noted earlier in the source reconstruction notes. The current source still stages `EV_DAMAGEPLUM` through `LE_SCOREPLUM` because the retail queued world-marker record type was unnamed; these three promotions anchor the real allocator/update/draw trio without forcing unstable struct-field names beyond what HLIL already shows.
- Before this round, the current cgame map held `829` named addresses: `728 / 751` committed Ghidra functions (`96.9%`) plus `101` HLIL-only anchors for `829 / 852` combined committed anchors (`97.3%`). After this round, the map holds `832` named addresses: `731 / 751` committed Ghidra functions (`97.3%`) plus the same `101` HLIL-only anchors for `832 / 852` combined committed anchors (`97.7%`).

### Retail Screen-Damage / Big-Explode Tracer Sweep

- This pass promotes two more committed cgame starts from two compact retail holdouts: corrected synthetic `0x1000E9C0 -> CG_DrawJoinGameMenu` and exact `0x10013E60 -> CG_SpawnBigExplodeTracer`.
- `0x1000E9C0` was first treated as the old source-era `CG_DrawScreenDamage` slot because the committed `CG_Draw2D` decompile reaches it from the same broad HUD corridor. The corrected retail owner below is `CG_DrawJoinGameMenu`: string/menu evidence ties the helper to the spectator `joingame_menu` root, while visible damage feedback lives on the first-person sprite path in `cg_screen.c`.
- `0x10013E60` is the exact retail `CG_SpawnBigExplodeTracer` producer under the already-mapped synthetic `CG_SpawnBigExplodeEffects`. The call graph is one-to-one: the combined big-explode helper runs the same 36-iteration randomized tracer loop as current `cg_effects.c`, and this callee matches the public per-tracer body by allocating one `LE_BIGEXPLODE_TRACER`, keeping `LEF_PUFF_DONT_SCALE`, seeding the delayed lifetime and `TR_QL_ACCEL` timing, applying the fixed downward `posTrajExtra`, and mirroring the same sprite-shader/radius setup on the refEntity.

The effects side now names the exact tracer producer rather than only the fused wrapper and the local-entity consumer, and the HUD side records the retail repurposing of the old 2D screen-damage slot before the final stats/join-game overlay sweep corrects the stable symbol name.

### Retail Team-Chat / Vignette / Crosshair-Color Sweep

- `0x1004A1B0` is the exact retail `CG_AddToTeamChat` slot rather than another print-stack wrapper. The call graph is narrow: `CG_PlayVoiceChat` reaches it only for voice chats that should also echo text, and HLIL preserves the legacy team-chat ring implementation that the current source no longer carries inline. The function wraps at 79 characters, propagates Quake color escapes across wrapped segments, writes each completed line into the dedicated team-chat ring, and stamps the paired time array before advancing the cursor.
- `0x1000CA90` is the exact `CG_GetCrosshairTeamVitalColor` helper under the same-team crosshair-name path. HLIL matches the source routine instruction-for-instruction: it clamps non-positive `maxValue` to `100`, computes the low/high ramp for below-max versus overstacked values, fixes red at `1.0`, and writes the caller-supplied alpha into the final RGBA tuple used by the teammate health and armor labels.
- `0x10009D60` is a compact fullscreen vignette painter beneath `CG_Draw2D`, and the public source no longer exposes it as a named standalone function. HLIL only runs the leaf when the cached `cg_vignette` state is enabled, draws the registered `gfx/misc/vignette` shader across the full 640x480 screen via `CG_DrawPic`, and the surrounding `CG_DrawActive` control flow calls it immediately before tailcalling into the main 2D HUD pass when the browser overlay is inactive, so `CG_DrawScreenVignette` is the narrow stable synthetic name.

### Retail Team-Relation / Domination-Billboard Sweep

- This pass promotes four more committed cgame starts: synthetic `0x10015190 -> CG_ResolveClientModelColorBytes`, synthetic `0x1002DFF0 -> CG_AlignTextX`, synthetic `0x1003CAD0 -> CG_IsFriendlyClientTeam`, and synthetic `0x10041060 -> CG_QueueDominationPointBillboard`.
- `0x1003CAD0` is the shared friendly-team predicate that retail routes through both the player-model color path and the already-mapped weapon-color helpers. HLIL reduces the active gametype, FFA/team cases, and local-team comparison into a single boolean gate, so the stable role is "should this client be treated as friendly for color selection" rather than a narrower one-off render condition.
- `0x10015190` is the matching packed player-model color resolver beneath the `CG_Player` render corridor. The leaf calls `CG_IsFriendlyClientTeam`, selects the self / friendly / enemy override banks, and writes four packed bytes into the caller buffer used later by the player-model submission path; it is distinct from the parallel weapon-color helpers already mapped at `0x1004F280` and `0x1004F420`, but clearly part of the same retail color-override family.
- `0x1002DFF0` is a smaller sibling of `CG_AlignTextInRectX`, not another generic text-measure thunk. HLIL shows it measuring the supplied string through `CG_Text_GetExtents` and then shifting the caller's x origin left by half-width or full width for center/right alignment, with no surrounding rect translation. That keeps the synthetic name narrow and avoids overstating it as the larger rect-aware helper already mapped at `0x1002E050`.
- `0x10041060` is the queued Domination overlay half of the retail `CG_DominationPoint` split. The body selects from the four registered `gfx/2d/dom_point/dom_cap_*`, `dom_def_*`, `dom_cap_*_dist`, and `dom_def_*_dist` shader families according to the point state, allocates a queued world marker through `CG_AllocQueuedWorldMarker`, and publishes the Domination point origin plus billboard lifetime and color state. The current source keeps the broader behavior under `CG_DominationPoint`, but the shipping DLL factors this billboard/marker work into its own leaf.

### Retail Weapon-Token Parser Sweep

- This pass promotes two more committed cgame starts: synthetic `0x10001DF0 -> CG_StartingWeaponIndexFromToken` and synthetic `0x10001E50 -> CG_ParseDamagePlumWeaponMask`.
- `0x10001DF0` is the narrow queued-primary parser beneath the retail starting-weapon HUD path. HLIL parses a single token from the caller-supplied string, walks the shared retail weapon-token table at `data_10079094`, and returns the first matching table ordinal as a 1-based icon-slot index. The only committed caller pushes `cg_weaponPrimaryQueued` before invoking the helper and then stores the result in `data_10a9c7a4`, which the already-recovered starting-weapon drawer immediately consumes for the highlighted primary-weapon icon.
- `0x10001E50` is the paired multi-token mask parser used by the retail damage-plum seam. HLIL loops through up to sixteen parsed tokens, compares each token against the same retail weapon-token table, rotates a one-hot bit across the table order, and ORs matching bits into the returned mask. The only committed caller is the already-recovered `EV_DAMAGEPLUM` world-marker producer at `0x10013660`, which gates the local damage-number spawn on the returned weapon bitmask, so the stable role is a damage-plum weapon-filter parser rather than a generic loadout helper.
- These two promotions also clarify a useful retail divergence from the current GPL-side reconstruction. The present source keeps `CG_StartingWeaponFromToken` and `CG_ParseDamagePlumWeaponValue` as separate text-to-weapon helpers, but the shipping DLL factors them around a shared retail token table and returns either a starting-weapon display index or a bitmask, depending on the caller.

After this round, the map holds `848` named addresses: `747 / 751` committed Ghidra functions (`99.5%`) plus the same `101` HLIL-only anchors for `848 / 852` combined committed anchors (`99.5%`).

### Retail Flag-Predicate / Invulnerability / Crosshair-Hit Sweep

- This pass promotes four more committed cgame starts: synthetic `0x10001000 -> BG_IsRedBlueFlagItem`, exact `0x10003F50 -> PM_InvulnerabilityMove`, synthetic `0x1000C0A0 -> CG_ApplyCrosshairHitFeedback`, and synthetic `0x10008780 -> CG_Text_PaintNoAdjust`.
- `0x10001000` is the tiny retail flag predicate under the item-touch prediction seam. HLIL only returns true when the supplied `bg_itemlist` row is an `IT_TEAM` item whose tag lands in the first two colored-flag slots, and the only committed caller is the already-recovered `CG_TouchItem` predictor path at `0x100443C0`, which uses that result to suppress the local predicted pickup flow for the red/blue CTF flags while leaving the other item classes on the normal `EV_ITEM_PICKUP` path. The current source still inlines a broader flag-special-case block in `cg_predict.c`, so the safest stable name here is a narrow synthetic item predicate.
- `0x10003F50` is the retail `PM_InvulnerabilityMove` boundary. `PM_Weapon` arms `PMF_USE_ITEM_HELD` for holdable tag `6`, the walk and grapple branches both fan into this helper under that exact gate, `PmoveSingle` clears the same replicated powerup slot each frame before movement begins, and HLIL for this leaf then seeds the active invulnerability state, applies the pitch-driven float / sink bias, drains the internal activation timer at `stats[STAT_PLAYER_ITEM_TIME]`, clears the pending holdable slot when the effect collapses with no recharge rate, and forces the special legs-animation branch while active.
- `0x1000C0A0` is a deliberate synthetic crosshair-hit feedback helper beneath `CG_DrawCrosshair`. HLIL reads the cached `cg_crosshairHitStyle`, `cg_crosshairHitTime`, and `cg_crosshairHitColor` state, scales the caller's width/height pair for the active hit window, and selects either one of the built-in retail color styles or the configured user hit-color palette before the main crosshair draw continues. The surrounding transition-playerstate seam at `0x10043B60` also stamps the matching hit timestamp and style payload, which confirms this is the display-side consumer of the retail hit-indicator state rather than a generic crosshair color helper.
- `0x10008780` is not another semantic text subsystem, just the last retail convenience wrapper around the main painter. HLIL ignores the decompiler's dead leading register argument, hardcodes `adjust = 0`, preserves the caller-supplied text, limit, style, color, and scale inputs, and tail-calls `CG_Text_Paint`. The surrounding callers are exactly the many HUD and ownerdraw sites that always render zero-adjust text, so a narrow synthetic wrapper name is safer than pretending the DLL still exposes a distinct GPL function here.

### Retail Stats / Join-Game Overlay Final Sweep

- This pass resolves the last remaining cgame mapping seam in the retail HUD/browser overlay cluster. It promotes one more HLIL-only helper, `0x1000E930 -> CG_CloseRetailCommandCaptureOverlay`, and also corrects two earlier over-narrow labels: `0x1000E320` is the retail `stats_menu` drawer rather than a standalone icon, and `0x1000E9C0` is the spectator-only `joingame_menu` drawer rather than a retained `CG_DrawScreenDamage` leaf.
- The first correction is grounded in both the committed string table and the shipped HUD asset. The retail string block carries adjacent `stats_menu` and `joingame_menu` roots, `ui/ingamestats.menu` defines a `stats_menu` overlay whose body is exactly the vertical weapon-accuracy panel, and HLIL for `0x1000E320` both throttles the `acc` client command and paints the cached root tied to that request latch. That is a real menu-root draw helper, not just a small HUD icon.
- The second correction is the same style of evidence chain. `ui/intro.menu` defines the spectator `joingame_menu` root, and HLIL for `0x1000E9C0` activates and paints the cached second overlay root only while the local client remains on the spectator team, otherwise immediately dismissing the broader capture state. This means retail repurposed the old source-era `CG_DrawScreenDamage` slot in `CG_Draw2D` for the join-game overlay, while visible damage feedback moved onto the first-person sprite path instead of remaining a dedicated 2D draw helper.
- The new HLIL-only `0x1000E930` helper then closes the last unresolved retail-only `CG_EventHandling(5)` branch. The body is the close-only sibling of `CG_ClearRetailCommandCaptureState`: it closes the active cgame-owned overlay when present and clears the cgame keycatcher bit, but deliberately leaves the broader capture latch and its timestamp untouched. That makes the retail-only event id a close-overlay variant rather than another gameplay HUD mode.
- With this pass, no unresolved cgame naming gaps remain in the current committed corpus plus promoted HLIL seams. The only remaining cgame open items are corpus-maintenance questions outside the live symbol map itself.

The blinking branch calls the shader registration callback for `gfx/2d/net.tga` and immediately draws it at `592,432` sized `48x48`, so the source now mirrors the helper body while preserving the separate `disconnected` preload.

- The committed Ghidra callback slab wires `CG_OwnerDraw`, then `CG_GetValue`, then `CG_OwnerDrawVisible`, with `CG_OwnerDrawWidth` later in the same display context. Current source keeps that bridge shape in `cg_main.c::CG_InitDisplayContext`.

The legacy `CG_SELECTEDPLAYER_ARMOR` / `CG_SELECTEDPLAYER_HEALTH` ids stay outside the callback, matching the no-op legacy selected-player ownerdraw corridor.
- The display-context parity suite now guards both sides mechanically: the raw Ghidra assignments in `FUN_10029210`, the source `cgDC` callback order, the six menu ownerdraw ids, and the absence of selected-player/team-player value lookups inside `CG_GetValue`.

### Retail Ownerdraw Width Surface Sweep

Every other ownerdraw id returns zero.
- `cg_main.c::CG_OwnerDrawWidth` now mirrors that callback surface directly. The earlier source-only width handling for timers, round labels, overtime, race text, health/armor, and red/blue team names was removed from the callback while leaving the actual draw helpers untouched.

### Retail Player-Count Tournament Cap Sweep

### Retail Game Limit Cache And Centering Sweep

### Retail Match End Condition Sentence Sweep

- This pass keeps map coverage unchanged at `854 / 854` combined committed anchors (`100.0%`) and tightens `0x10034280 -> CG_DrawMatchEndCondition`.
- HLIL does not report a dynamic post-match reason such as `Time limit hit` or `Frag limit hit`; it selects one of nine fixed instructional sentences: fastest Race time, most flag captures/rounds/highest score within the time limit, first to reach capture/mercy/round/score limit, or highest score at game end.
- Source reconstruction now mirrors the retail branch shape: Race bypasses the time-limit check, CTF chooses capture versus mercy based on whether either team reached `capturelimit`, Clan Arena uses the round-limit text, Domination and Attack and Defend use the score-limit text, and all other non-time-limit modes fall back to the highest-score-at-end sentence.
- The ownerdraw helper now draws directly at `rect->x, rect->y`, matching the HLIL paint call, and the dispatcher no longer passes `text_x` / `text_y` into this leaf.
- The ownerdraw-text parity suite now checks the retail string table and backing globals, the source branch buckets, and the absence of the old source-only result strings and helper stack.

### Retail Gametype And Match-State Baseline Sweep

- This pass keeps map coverage unchanged at `854 / 854` combined committed anchors (`100.0%`) and tightens the adjacent `0x10034C20 -> CG_DrawGameType` and `0x10034360 -> CG_DrawMatchState` wrappers.
- HLIL for `CG_DrawGameType` takes the ownerdraw alignment argument, measures text only for `align == 1`, subtracts half the measured width from the rect x anchor, and paints the gametype string at the supplied rect y. There is no right-alignment branch and no shader dependency in the retail leaf.
- HLIL for `CG_DrawMatchState` likewise paints the uppercase phase banner at `arg1[1]`, not at `rect->y + rect->h`; the neighboring `CG_DrawGameStatus` baseline remains `rect->y + rect->h` and was left intact because its HLIL explicitly adds `arg1[3]`.
- Source now passes `align` into `CG_DrawGameType`, removes the stale shader argument from that wrapper, uses center-only width adjustment, and moves both `CG_DrawGameType` and `CG_DrawMatchState` onto the retail raw-y paint origin. The parity suites now guard those HLIL branches and reject the old `rect->y + rect->h` paths for these two leaves.
